<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Busiest_US_airports_by_total_passenger_boardings">Busiest US airports by total passenger boardings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Busiest US airports by total passenger boardings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The FAA uses passenger boarding for a full calendar year to determine <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airport_Improvement_Program" title="Airport Improvement Program">Airport Improvement Program</a> (AIP) entitlements.<sup id="cite_ref-CY14-2_1-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States#cite_note-CY14-2-1">[1]</a></sup> 
The term <i>hub</i> is used by the FAA to identify very busy commercial service airports. For instance, large hubs are those airports that each account for at least one percent of total U.S. passenger enplanements. Medium hubs are defined as airports that each account for between 0.25 percent and one percent of the total passenger enplanements.
</p><p>The 30 large hubs move 70% of the passengers with a traffic increasing by 2.5% from 2016 to 2017, while the 31 medium hubs grew by 5.2% and sixteen airports lost airline services between 2014 and 2018, from 445 to 429.
Mainline carriers are up-gauging their fleet while <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scope_clause" title="Scope clause">scope clauses</a> regional aircraft operations and turboprops and 50-seat <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_jet" title="Regional jet">regional jets</a> are abandoned: aircraft with 50 seats or fewer represented 30% of domestic departures and 12% of seats offered in 2014, falling to 19% in 2018 and 7% of seats.
Accounting for 18% of passenger traffic, medium hubs stimulate point-to-point services like for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a>, operating at 29, carrying most mainline passengers at 24 and more than half at 10.
Southwest’s first-quarter of 2018 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cost_per_Available_Seat_Mile" class="mw-redirect" title="Cost per Available Seat Mile">CASM</a> excluding fuel and special charges was 8.65 cents, roughly equivalent to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue Airways</a> and more than 20% lower than <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, while <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultra-low_cost_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultra-low cost airline">ULCCs</a> are lower like <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit Airlines</a> at 5.83 cents while <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier Airlines</a>' is undisclosed.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek23jul2018_2-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States#cite_note-AvWeek23jul2018-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span id="46_busiest_US_airports_by_total_passenger_traffic_.282016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="46_busiest_US_airports_by_total_passenger_traffic_(2016)">46 busiest US airports by total passenger traffic (2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 46 busiest US airports by total passenger traffic (2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Listed according to data compiled by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airports_Council_International" title="Airports Council International">Airports Council International</a> North America, and ranked according to total passengers during 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI_15-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States#cite_note-ACI-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>All 46 airports on this list are also featured on the FAA list, but the order varies. The FAA ranks by passengers boarding. ACI ranks by sum of boarding, disembarking, and flying through without leaving airplane. The statistics are slightly more than twice as high.
</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable jquery-tablesorter">

<h2><span id="20_busiest_US_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic_.282017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="20_busiest_US_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic_(2017)"><span id="20_busiest_US_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic"></span>20 busiest US airports by international passenger traffic (2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 20 busiest US airports by international passenger traffic (2017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Listed according to data compiled by the Office of Aviation Analysis, part of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">United States Department of Transportation</a>, and ranked according to total international passengers during 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States#cite_note-autogenerated1-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span id="10_busiest_airports_in_the_US_by_total_cargo_throughput_.282015.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="10_busiest_airports_in_the_US_by_total_cargo_throughput_(2015)">10 busiest airports in the US by total cargo throughput (2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 10 busiest airports in the US by total cargo throughput (2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States" title="List of largest cargo airports in the United States">List of largest cargo airports in the United States</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States_Map.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="Largest cargo airports in the United States Map.jpeg" src="./aa_files/Largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States_Map.jpeg.jpeg" width="300" height="225" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States_Map.jpeg/450px-Largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States_Map.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States_Map.jpeg/600px-Largest_cargo_airports_in_the_United_States_Map.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a></div>
<p>Listed according to data compiled by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and ranked according to total cargo throughput in pounds during 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
